  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ebceeb0c-0134-4d2d-a57e-4945c699741b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer14812046224145310482">She is the girl with the dragon tattoo—a genius hacker and uncompromising misfit. He is a crusading journalist whose championing of the truth often brings him to the brink of prosecution.<br/><br/>Late one night, Blomkvist receives a phone call from a source claiming to have information vital to the United States. The source has been in contact with a young female superhacker—a hack</span>
  <span id="freeText14812046224145310482" style="display:none">She is the girl with the dragon tattoo—a genius hacker and uncompromising misfit. He is a crusading journalist whose championing of the truth often brings him to the brink of prosecution.<br /><br />Late one night, Blomkvist receives a phone call from a source claiming to have information vital to the United States. The source has been in contact with a young female superhacker—a hacker resembling someone Blomkvist knows all too well. The implications are staggering. Blomkvist, in desperate need of a scoop for Millennium, turns to Salander for help. She, as usual, has her own agenda. The secret they are both chasing is at the center of a tangled web of spies, cybercriminals, and governments around the world, and someone is prepared to kill to protect it . . . <br /><br />The duo who captivated millions of readers in <i>The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo, The Girl Who Played with Fire</i>, and <i>The Girl Who Kicked the Hornet’s Nest</i> join forces again in this adrenaline-charged, uniquely of-the-moment thriller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14812046224145310482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">** With glittering eyes and an everlasting smile, each of them (the people who rated the book) says “I liked, I mean loved, these books so much that I<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">** With glittering eyes and an everlasting smile, each of them (the people who rated the book) says “I liked, I mean loved, these books so much that I am going to love each and every one that follows as well!!” **<br /><br />And this is what I call the Overly Attached Fan Syndrome ^^<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">People are really weird. Someone gave it one star and left a comment saying, "I will never read this book." I mean, they rated a book they never read.<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">People are really weird. Someone gave it one star and left a comment saying, "I will never read this book." I mean, they rated a book they never read. WHY do that???<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_more_filters_span_tip_491').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1383876547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1383876547" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1383876547?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=nordic-noir">nordic-noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1383876547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6093482900293651360"><b>”It’s always the wrong people who have the guilty conscience. Those who are really responsible for suffering in the world couldn’t care less. It’s the ones fighting for good who are consumed by remorse.”</b><br/><br/>David Lagercrantz, a novelist and journalist, was asked to assume responsibility for the continuation of a trilogy of novels that frankly took the publishing industry by storm. The books left readers stunned with the marvelous insanity of the writing. More importantly Stieg Larsson created a char</span>
  <span id="freeText6093482900293651360" style="display:none"><b>”It’s always the wrong people who have the guilty conscience. Those who are really responsible for suffering in the world couldn’t care less. It’s the ones fighting for good who are consumed by remorse.”</b><br /><br />David Lagercrantz, a novelist and journalist, was asked to assume responsibility for the continuation of a trilogy of novels that frankly took the publishing industry by storm. The books left readers stunned with the marvelous insanity of the writing. More importantly Stieg Larsson created a character who is forever immortalized as one of the greatest anti-heroes to ever step out of the pages of a book. <br /><br /><b>Lisbeth Salander</b><br /><br />It doesn’t surprise me that Lagercrantz is a little afraid of her. Who isn’t? His fear might be reflected in the fact that she is a shadowy figure in the book until about halfway through when she answers a call from Mikael Blomkvist. <br /><br /><b>”Shut up and listen,” she said.</b><br /><br />Ahhh, yes, that’s my girl. <br /><br />She doesn’t look like much, just an androgynous girl? with piercings, tattoos, and strange hair. She is undersized, but bristles with attitude. The outward appearance is not just for show...it is bone deep. She is blessed/cursed with a photographic memory. She doesn’t have the patience or sympathy for stupidity. She has no time for social niceties. If you were her “friend,” you would see her only when she wanted to be seen. If you are involved with her sexually, you will find that you are not really “involved” with her at all. <br /><br />But the sex...well...is by all accounts...fantastic.<br /><br />If you are someone who gets aroused by beating up women or children, you better pray to all that is holy that Salander doesn’t find out who you are because you will find yourself with her boot on your throat wondering how this diminutive creature incapacitated you so quickly. You’ll want to hurt her, but she is capable of not only hurting you physically, but also taking your whole identity away from you. <br /><br />Because...<br /><br />she is also a hacker. A vengeful hacker, but also a prideful hacker. When she gets the chance to hack the National Security Agency in Washington, D.C., she goes through their system like buttered bread. <br /><br /><b>All hell breaks loose. </b><br /><br />Lagercrantz might have underestimated just how much America would overreact to such a breach of security. In reality, Sweden might have found themselves invaded by Marines, tanks, and Apache helicopters as the Americans turned over every stone looking for someone with the hacker handle <b>WASP</b>. <br /><br />For the first part of the book, Lagercrantz puts Mikael Blomkvist center stage. It would make sense that he identifies with him since they share a similar profession. Not that I mind spending time with Mikael Blomkvist, if he were a real person, would give me hope for journalism. He is a person obsessed with the truth. Other journalists either revere him or hate him. He is a target for those that loath him. <i>”Your uncompromising attitude makes people feel pathetic. Your very existence reminds them just how much they’ve sold out, and the more you’re acclaimed, the punier they themselves appear. When it’s like that the only way they can fight back is by dragging you down.”</i><br /><br />Millennium, the magazine he founded, is in trouble. They had to sell out a portion of their ownership to keep the publication afloat, but now those same corporate people who bought them to add some integrity to their own list of titles suddenly want to compromise the integrity of Millennium by adding more human interest material. <br /><br />For me, now that I’m one of the owners of the publication I work for, the trials and tribulations of a magazine to keep up subscription levels hit home. Any softening of the economy turns subscription renewals into luxuries, not to mention all the competition from free publications online that also erode print subscriptions. <br /><br />So Blomkvist is in a funk; more is going wrong than is going right. He is spending most of his time, even the time he is supposed to be sleeping, reading Elizabeth George novels one after another. I can relate to that for there is nothing like escaping into the pages of a good book when life becomes <b>TOO BORING, TOO DEPRESSING, TOO REAL.</b><br /><br />A call from Frans Balder finally gets Mikael reinvigorated. Balder is a leading expert on Artificial General Intelligence or <i>”Something with the intelligence of a human being, but the speed and precision of a computer.”</i> <br /><br />The plot explodes. <br /><br />It doesn’t take long for Salander and Blomkvist to realize they are working the same problem from different ends of the stick. With her behind the scenes, beyond the law approach to finding out the truth and his unflinching, uncompromising need to expose hypocrisy, the duo form a team that scares everyone from criminal elements, to large corporations, to governments. Sometimes it is difficult to tell the difference between those elements. <br /><br />There is techno jargon, but Lagercrantz does a great job of explaining everything. He also does a fantastic job talking about autism and savant tendencies in socially compromised children. I thought it was cool that an autistic child becomes an important plotting device. Lagercrantz did not have access to the notes left by Stieg Larsson for continuing the story. This probably was more of a blessing than a curse. Larsson’s, long time girlfriend ( that term seems so out dating and doesn’t quite explain the situation), has been in a legal battle to obtain ownership or rights to Larsson’s unpublished works. It seems the Swedes, so advanced in so many ways, might be lagging behind in the common law aspect of inheritance. I believe that Lagercrantz by using the first three novels as his only source documentation kept himself from being hampered by Larsson in making this novel his own creation. <br /><br />I read this book in two days. I thought the plot was great. I thought the writing was very good, even if it did lack some of the flair that was such a Larsson trademark. It is hard to wear a dead man’s suit, but I have to say Lagercrantz, even if the jacket was too big in the shoulders or too short in the arms, still managed to make me believe that even as he left the funeral he was leading me back to a new beginning and creating a new life for characters that were relegated to retirement much too early. <br /><br />If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br />I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6093482900293651360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1355257132" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1355257132" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1355257132?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1355257132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13167319825520663503">Re/Read on Audio! <br/><br/>MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/09/the-girl-in-spiders-web-by-david.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455384695i/18096100._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I thought this book was wonderful! I have missed Lisbeth and Blomkvist for so long. I think the new author did a great job carrying on Stieg Larsson's series. <br/><br/>Lisbeth is one of the coolest women out there. I love her character, I love how smart she is, oh if I could be as smart as her. I do hate her past, but I am glad that she is a character that was written to rise above all of the horrible things that happened to her. <br/><br/>In this new book th</span>
  <span id="freeText13167319825520663503" style="display:none">Re/Read on Audio! <br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/09/the-girl-in-spiders-web-by-david.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455384695i/18096100._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I thought this book was wonderful! I have missed Lisbeth and Blomkvist for so long. I think the new author did a great job carrying on Stieg Larsson's series. <br><br>Lisbeth is one of the coolest women out there. I love her character, I love how smart she is, oh if I could be as smart as her. I do hate her past, but I am glad that she is a character that was written to rise above all of the horrible things that happened to her. <br><br>In this new book there is another scandal of sorts going on within a huge community of people. A lot of things going on in the hacker community, people stealing other people's work, killings, blackmail, a little boy with Autism, evilness and goodness. And of course Lisbeth is right in the middle of it all and she does her job as hard core as she always does. <br><br>In the beginning of the book the author does have Blomkvist thinking back on things that happened in the other three books, nothing real extensive but I thought it was a nice little add to the book. <br><br>I was very much intrigued and on the edge of my seat between the interactions with the little boy (August) and Lisbeth. She was so good with him and she did things that needed to be done and in her own wonderful way. I wanted to get up and cheer her on! I can't really say anything because there is no way I'm giving out any kind of spoiler for this book! <br><br>The ending was good and set up to possibly have more books, I hope there will be. <br><br>I personally loved the book, as I have mentioned. I know there are people that hate it or love it because it is Stieg's original characters. But for myself.. I think the family did a good job in choosing this man to start a continuation of what is a wonderful character.</span>

<div id="review_1384993085" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1384993085" />
    <a title="Brandon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon"><img alt="Brandon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603283104p2/3214163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1384993085?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandon" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon">Brandon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1384993085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6272266617537102782">The whole story behind the creation and release of The Girl in the Spider’s Web is actually somewhat disgusting. Series’ creator Stieg Larsson unexpectedly died from a heart attack in 2004, a year before the first novel in the Millennium trilogy was to be published. In the years that followed, the books enjoyed tremendous, widespread success as Larsson’s characters would grow a rabid fan base. Unfortunately for readers, the series would end after the publication of the third and final novel. Or </span>
  <span id="freeText6272266617537102782" style="display:none">The whole story behind the creation and release of The Girl in the Spider’s Web is actually somewhat disgusting. Series’ creator Stieg Larsson unexpectedly died from a heart attack in 2004, a year before the first novel in the Millennium trilogy was to be published. In the years that followed, the books enjoyed tremendous, widespread success as Larsson’s characters would grow a rabid fan base. Unfortunately for readers, the series would end after the publication of the third and final novel. Or would it?<br /><br />Despite having written a will years prior to his untimely death, it was not witnessed and having not married his long-time partner, his estate wound up in the hands of his estranged father and brother. Despite his partner claiming that Stieg would not want his work continued by another author, Larsson’s family hired David Lagercrantz, a Swedish journalist and crime writer in his own right, to pick up where Larsson left off.<br /><br />On one hand, it’s gross. This new novel appears as nothing more than an attempt to capitalize on the success of Steig’s work by his alienated family. However on the other hand, the duo of Blomkvist and Salander probably do have a lot left in the tank as well as an audience eager to gobble down new stories. The only question being, is Lagercrantz the right choice to take on these iconic characters or is The Girl in the Spider’s Web nothing more than glorified fan fiction?<br /><br />While I certainly wouldn’t label it fan fiction, I also wouldn’t put it on the same level as Larsson’s work (although, I did enjoy it more than Hornet’s Nest). Lagercrantz can appear to write a solid crime novel, but he’s missing that meandering style of writing that made the original trilogy special. I mean, come on – Blomkvist only made three sandwiches! I expected more from him.<br /><br />My biggest issue is in the lack of Lisbeth. It isn’t until after the first 100 pages that she’s really woven into the storyline and even then, she’s mostly used sporadically. While she’s integral to the central plot, she’s mostly spoken of by peripheral characters rather than having her own voice. The same issue arose when I was reading The Girl Who Played With Fire, where Lisbeth is “off-screen” for a good chunk of the story, but there ain’t no way I’m going to compare the explosiveness of her actions in that novel to this one, they’re not even in the same league.<br /><br />The incredible success of this novel in terms of sales (two hundred thousand copies moved in the first week alone) and positive critical reception should surely lead to a follow-up, although nothing is currently planned, however money is a powerful motivator.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6272266617537102782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1379783797" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379783797" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1379783797?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=reviewcopy">reviewcopy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1379783797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15963307380753074923">Despite concerns over whether Stieg Larsson's wishes were being honored by the publication of this book (based on reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10473353._There_Are_Things_I_Want_You_to_Know__about_Stieg_Larsson_and_Me' title='"There Are Things I Want You to Know" about Stieg Larsson and Me by Eva Gabrielsson' rel='nofollow noopener'>"There Are Things I Want You to Know" about Stieg Larsson and Me</a>), I decided to go ahead and try it. I loved the character of Lisbeth Salander and thought if it was done well, it might be worth it. You don't encounter many characters like her.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, I was supremely disappointed, so much so that I can't face going back to the book after making it halfway through the au</span>
  <span id="freeText15963307380753074923" style="display:none">Despite concerns over whether Stieg Larsson's wishes were being honored by the publication of this book (based on reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10473353._There_Are_Things_I_Want_You_to_Know__about_Stieg_Larsson_and_Me" title="&quot;There Are Things I Want You to Know&quot; about Stieg Larsson and Me by Eva Gabrielsson" rel="nofollow noopener">"There Are Things I Want You to Know" about Stieg Larsson and Me</a>), I decided to go ahead and try it. I loved the character of Lisbeth Salander and thought if it was done well, it might be worth it. You don't encounter many characters like her.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I was supremely disappointed, so much so that I can't face going back to the book after making it halfway through the audio. First of all, these are not the same characters of Lisbeth and Mikael that I know from the trilogy. Lisbeth seems to have reverted to one of two modes - sloppy hacker or hungover boxer - no depth, no motivation, nothing interesting. It could be that we reached the end of her story in the trilogy. Mikael is unmotivated too, can't stand to be at work and arriving late to the scene of an important crime that finally happens midway through the book. <br /><br />The author spends TOO much time describing things that don't matter - an hour (I listened to the audio) on the current status of Millennium, the news publication that Mikael has worked on; the storms, frequent descriptions; and Mikael's white fur coat. He hasn't bothered to explore the characters themselves. He touches on the subjects of autism and the singularity in halfhearted ways that the characters and the reader end up feeling less than inspired. (And really? Artificial intelligence? It isn't written about intelligently enough to feel like high stakes. This is set in the present day. If I wanted a thrilling read about AI and the singularity I would look for it in science fiction, where it is handled with interesting variations and frightening possibilities, NOT in a Swedish crime novel. It makes no sense.)<br /><br />I would be happy if someone came along who convinced me that this book turned a huge corner and I should have kept reading... but I doubt that will happen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15963307380753074923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8060405665404993832">The Millennium Series Book 5 came out this month....so I finally finished Book 4....which has been on my shelf since 2015.   <span id="freeText8060405665404993832" style="display:none">The Millennium Series Book 5 came out this month....so I finally finished Book 4....which has been on my shelf since 2015. I started and stopped a couple of times....It’s not a book that immediately grabs your attention... but once it gets going — it’s a full speed fast spinning ride. Hacker girl, Lisbeth, inscrutable, who is scheming follows her own timetable. She is chasing a web of spies, cyber criminals, and governments around the world. Blomkvist happens to be doing the same thing - and ( of course ) needs Lisbeth’s help.<br /><br />I’m not sure what the mixed reviews are about ( the fuss?) with book 5...but in book 4....<br />......”The Girl in the Spider’s Web”.....Lisbeth Salander and Mikael Blomkvist still have that robustness toughness team vitality— often at arms length ( agony for me - as I love it when they are in the same room)—but by the end of this novel, I easily accepted that Steig Larson’s characters are in good hands with author David Lagercrantz. <br /><br />A little dialogue sample of what I love when Lisbeth and Blomkvist are together:<br /> “Are you angry with me?” he said<br /> “Quite”<br /> “Why is that?”<br /> “Salander took a step forward, her face shining and pale, and he remembered her gunshot wound”. <br /> “Because I come to visit, and there’s no one at home,” she said. He walked towards her”. <br /> “That’s a bit of a scandal, isn’t it?”, he said<br /> “I’d say so.”<br /> “What if I ask you in now?”<br /> “Then I suppose I’ll have to accept”. <br /> “In that case, welcome”, he said, and for the first time in ages a broad smile spread across his face”.<br /> “A star fell outside in the night sky”.<br /><br />It was a joy to be back in Lisbeth-land!!!</span>

<div id="review_1354769259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354769259" />
    <a title="Skip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1389748-skip"><img alt="Skip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231161516p2/1389748.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1354769259?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skip" href="/user/show/1389748-skip">Skip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1389748-skip?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1389748-skip?shelf=foreign-translated">foreign-translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1389748-skip?shelf=goodreads-giveaway">goodreads-giveaway</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354769259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15850905047975684646">Just as true Deadheads do not appreciate Trey Anastasio playing Jerry Garcia's lead guitar or singing his songs, David Lagercrantz is not Stieg Larsson. He has a different writing style, but Lisbeth Salander remains one of the most innovative and iconic characters in modern fiction: an antisocial goth female hacker, fighting with all her substantial might against injustice, both perceived or actual. The novel gets off to a rather slow start, with a Swedish professor abandoning his quest for self</span>
  <span id="freeText15850905047975684646" style="display:none">Just as true Deadheads do not appreciate Trey Anastasio playing Jerry Garcia's lead guitar or singing his songs, David Lagercrantz is not Stieg Larsson. He has a different writing style, but Lisbeth Salander remains one of the most innovative and iconic characters in modern fiction: an antisocial goth female hacker, fighting with all her substantial might against injustice, both perceived or actual. The novel gets off to a rather slow start, with a Swedish professor abandoning his quest for self learning artificial intelligence to take custody of his autistic son, August. All is not well at <i>Millenium</i> magazine and Mikael Blomkvist is under attack from many sides. The professor contacts Blomkvist as he is advised of threats to his life, setting off a series of escalating events, forcing Lisbeth to intervene with her usual forceful assistance. She rescues August and somehow manages to connect with him, continuing the breakthrough made by his father. There is substantial action in the second half of the novel, as matters escalate and an old adversary re-emerges from the darkness. <u>More please</u>.<br />----------------<br />9/17/2015 Addendum: I won a Goodreads giveaway for this book -- hooray!! Since it has not arrived yet, it did not affect this review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15850905047975684646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1277746949" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277746949" />
    <a title="Hayat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6116230-hayat"><img alt="Hayat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420050859p2/6116230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277746949?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hayat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hayat" href="/user/show/6116230-hayat">Hayat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6116230-hayat?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6116230-hayat?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6116230-hayat?shelf=family-relationships">family-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6116230-hayat?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277746949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2780540954105869397"><b>Update: read in August 2015 but decided to update in January 2016 </b> <br/><br/>I read the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7822895.The_Millennium_Trilogy' title='The Millennium Trilogy by Stieg Larsson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Millennium Trilogy</a> in anticipation of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25074850.The_Girl_in_the_Spider_s_Web' title='The Girl in the Spider's Web by David Lagercrantz' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl in the Spider's Web</a> and as soon as it was out I began reading it with a lot of excitement and a little apprehension, just in case the new author doesn't live up to or come close to the writing talents of <b>Stieg Larsson.</b><br/><br/>Well, clearly David Lagercrantz is no Stieg Larsson and everything I loved about <b>The Millennium Trilogy</b> was missing here. The plot was slow and tedious, </span>
  <span id="freeText2780540954105869397" style="display:none"><b>Update: read in August 2015 but decided to update in January 2016 </b> <br><br>I read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7822895.The_Millennium_Trilogy" title="The Millennium Trilogy by Stieg Larsson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Millennium Trilogy</a> in anticipation of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25074850.The_Girl_in_the_Spider_s_Web" title="The Girl in the Spider's Web by David Lagercrantz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Spider's Web</a> and as soon as it was out I began reading it with a lot of excitement and a little apprehension, just in case the new author doesn't live up to or come close to the writing talents of <b>Stieg Larsson.</b><br><br>Well, clearly David Lagercrantz is no Stieg Larsson and everything I loved about <b>The Millennium Trilogy</b> was missing here. The plot was slow and tedious, Lisbeth Salander was absent from a good portion of the book and when she turned up her character was different and not as well thought out or intriguing. <b>Lisbeth</b> is my favourite character, the driving force of the series and the reason I love the trilogy so much but in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25074850.The_Girl_in_the_Spider_s_Web" title="The Girl in the Spider's Web by David Lagercrantz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Spider's Web</a> she lost that unique element that made her Lisbeth Salander. Her narrative was different, her actions didn't make sense and there were lots of little things that didn't add up about her reactions. She was a caricature of her former self. <br><br>I found myself Skimming due to boredom until things picked up near the end but by then I was ready for it to end. I actually got the audiobook too but nothing changed. I'm a huge fan of <b>The Millennium Trilogy</b> and I've read it several times but this book didn't feel like a continuation of Stieg Larsson's trilogy. Everything was out of sync. I guess this shows that you can't rope in another writer to continue a deceased authors work. You can't replicate the original authors style, experience, knowledge and all the complexities that went into developing and writing The Millennium Trilogy. I'll probably reread this book sometime in the future just to see if my opinion of it changes but I doubt it will. Still, I'm willing to give it a second chance just to be fair to David Lagercrantz and in appreciation of the effort it took to write <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25074850.The_Girl_in_the_Spider_s_Web" title="The Girl in the Spider's Web by David Lagercrantz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Spider's Web</a>.<br><br><br><b>****Before publication in May 2015.****</b><br><br>OMG!!! I just found out my favourite series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7822895.The_Millennium_Trilogy" title="The Millennium Trilogy by Stieg Larsson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Millennium Trilogy</a> by Stieg Larssonis is being continued by a <b>new author!!!</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424549728ra/13776111.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm so happy and so bloody scared it is all going to go wrong! I both hate and love this!!<br><br>Oh who am I kidding! I need <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25074850.The_Girl_in_the_Spider_s_Web" title="The Girl in the Spider's Web by David Lagercrantz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Spider’s Web</a> right now!! September is too faraway.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403010552ra/10025572.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2780540954105869397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1463159105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1463159105" />
    <a title="Katie B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b"><img alt="Katie B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469412116p2/49444196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1463159105?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie B" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b">Katie B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857055323" href="/book/show/28549392-girl-in-the-spiders-web-export">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=sweden">sweden</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=autism">autism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1463159105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2125026952464265872">3.5 stars<br/><br/>I went into this with low expectations given it wasn't written by the author of the previous three books. I think it is such a huge undertaking to jump into a beloved series and attempt to duplicate the author's voice. While there are definitely some flaws it is a decent thriller and not some horrible attempt at fan fiction.<br/><br/>I enjoyed revisiting Blomkvist and Salander's world although the first half of the book really suffers by bouncing around between way too many characters. However, i</span>
  <span id="freeText2125026952464265872" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />I went into this with low expectations given it wasn't written by the author of the previous three books. I think it is such a huge undertaking to jump into a beloved series and attempt to duplicate the author's voice. While there are definitely some flaws it is a decent thriller and not some horrible attempt at fan fiction.<br /><br />I enjoyed revisiting Blomkvist and Salander's world although the first half of the book really suffers by bouncing around between way too many characters. However, it's easy to develop an emotional attachment to one of the new characters, an autistic child, and it's really hard not to get caught up in the story. <br /><br />I thought for the most part the author captured the general spirit of the series but I never felt like I was getting the full Blomkvist or Salander. With Salander in particular, it felt like the author was holding back a little and we were only getting about 85% of the character featured in previous books. It felt like Lisbeth lite so to speak, but I guess that is more preferably than the author going too far and turning her into some awful caricature. <br /><br />I have mixed feelings about the last few pages of the book, but overall I was satisfied with the author's attempt at continuing the series and will eventually check out the next book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2125026952464265872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1454214046" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454214046" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1454214046?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454214046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2040057553621764468">Stieg Larrson is dead, alas.<br/><br/>David Lagercrantz was granted a blessing and a curse. A blessing in the sense that he gets to write another Lisbeth and Mikael novel, a series with a worldwide following that will certainly sell and most definitely get a lot of attention.<br/><br/>A curse because he takes the stage after a phenomenal opening act, a lamentable position. Rumor has it that Larrson’s partner was far from pleased about his selection by the literary executor as the writer to take over. Readers who di</span>
  <span id="freeText2040057553621764468" style="display:none">Stieg Larrson is dead, alas.<br><br>David Lagercrantz was granted a blessing and a curse. A blessing in the sense that he gets to write another Lisbeth and Mikael novel, a series with a worldwide following that will certainly sell and most definitely get a lot of attention.<br><br>A curse because he takes the stage after a phenomenal opening act, a lamentable position. Rumor has it that Larrson’s partner was far from pleased about his selection by the literary executor as the writer to take over. Readers who dislike the book, and some will be relentlessly critical, will blame this new author. Those who just don’t like the book have an easy excuse.<br><br>Lagercrantz’ unenviable task, or golden opportunity, is to craft a new novel that stays true to the vision of Larrson the creator, revisits two of the most compelling characters in modern fiction, spins a crisp, intelligent thriller that will draw in fans and capture the attention of new readers, and does so with a fresh voice, paying homage to Larrson’s talent while putting ink on a work that is his.<br><br>For the most part, he succeeds admirably.<br><br>The Girl in the Spider's Web, the 2015 novel that takes up where the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6892870.The_Girl_Who_Kicked_the_Hornet_s_Nest__Millennium___3_" title="The Girl Who Kicked the Hornet's Nest (Millennium, #3) by Stieg Larsson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl Who Kicked the Hornet's Nest</a> (2007) left off, brings back Sweden’s most famous journalist and the world’s most iconic hacker for another thrilling adventure of exposed crime and wrongs righted. <br><br>Though it lacks the edgy chill of Larrson’s methodical delivery, Spider’s Web moves forward with verve and style.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504787698i/23816053._SY540_.jpg" width="156" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2040057553621764468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1375877042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1375877042" />
    <a title="Shannelle Lamour :)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42075915-shannelle-lamour"><img alt="Shannelle Lamour :)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434620467p2/42075915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1375877042?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannelle Lamour :)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannelle Lamour :)" href="/user/show/42075915-shannelle-lamour">Shannelle Lamour :)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1375877042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1150743926344900694">I'm sorry but no... I was super excited to read this to the point that I may have built it up in my head, and when it failed to deliver it made it that much more dissapointing. <br/><br/>Lisbeths character in the first three books was so fluid that she became such a believable person with all her quirks, silence, and way of behaving that were always so consistent. but in this book I caught myself at least fifteen plus times thinking 'Salander would never have said that'. It at times made for a frustrating</span>
  <span id="freeText1150743926344900694" style="display:none">I'm sorry but no... I was super excited to read this to the point that I may have built it up in my head, and when it failed to deliver it made it that much more dissapointing. <br /><br />Lisbeths character in the first three books was so fluid that she became such a believable person with all her quirks, silence, and way of behaving that were always so consistent. but in this book I caught myself at least fifteen plus times thinking 'Salander would never have said that'. It at times made for a frustrating read as I was constantly comparing the trilogy against this fourth book and always coming to the conclusion that its nothing like the first three. given the new author that's not surprising. its just extremely, dare I say it again, dissapointing. <br /><br />I loved Steig's writing style. His plot progression was great. I had to put this book down repeatedly due to being overwhelmed with information packed in a few sentences that would have by Steig been strategically placed through a few pages. It took me countless tries to finish this book. No offense to David, but maybe I should of left the story finished at book three. It felt like characters personalities were changed to adapt this new author. Some may argue that's to be expected considering Steig and David are two different people and will think different ways, but when trying to carry on a already stellar trilogy, I would have thought that enough research would have gone into it for Lisbeth and Blomkvist to be the same people they were throughout the first three books. <br /><br /><br />Like I said, disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1150743926344900694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1934592659" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1934592659" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1934592659?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=9-read-2017-03-march">9-read-2017-03-march</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=3-multi-book-series">3-multi-book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1934592659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17717263843317583025">3 stars to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/242659.David_Lagercrantz' title='David Lagercrantz' rel='nofollow noopener'>David Lagercrantz</a>'s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25074850.The_Girl_in_the_Spider_s_Web__Millennium___4_' title='The Girl in the Spider's Web (Millennium, #4) by David Lagercrantz' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl in the Spider's Web</a>, the fourth book in the "Millenium" thriller series, written by a new author given the original, Steig Larsson, passed away several years ago. While the book carries on with great characters and a similar style, it wasn't as satisfying as the originals. But who can resist Blomkvist and Lisbeth -- you can't NOT read it!<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Story</u>
</b><br/>As readers come to know of this series of books, the plots are incredibly complex, intense and twisty. From a b</span>
  <span id="freeText17717263843317583025" style="display:none">3 stars to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/242659.David_Lagercrantz" title="David Lagercrantz" rel="nofollow noopener">David Lagercrantz</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25074850.The_Girl_in_the_Spider_s_Web__Millennium___4_" title="The Girl in the Spider's Web (Millennium, #4) by David Lagercrantz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Spider's Web</a>, the fourth book in the "Millenium" thriller series, written by a new author given the original, Steig Larsson, passed away several years ago. While the book carries on with great characters and a similar style, it wasn't as satisfying as the originals. But who can resist Blomkvist and Lisbeth -- you can't NOT read it!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Story</u>
</b><br />As readers come to know of this series of books, the plots are incredibly complex, intense and twisty. From a basic point of view, several hackers have started infiltrating the NSA after learning about a conspiracy between different groups to buy and sell secrets about each other's companies. The government is involved, trying to keep it running and trying to stop it, as well as several public companies involved in building new technology that ultimately will be the destruction of mankind should machines be able to build machines and think as sentient beings<br /><br />Pushing that all to the side, the plot is about a professor who takes back his autistic son from his ex-wife and her new husband (who is abusing the young boy). When some members of the conspiracy group ultimately realize that the professor is the technologist who has the AI programs they are all after, and he's potentially going to rat out the truth of what's been happening to Blomkvist, someone orders a hit and the professor is killed minutes before telling his story. His young son witnesses the execution and the hunt begins. Lisbeth is involved in the hacking group and works through a secret computer program to help Blomkvist save the boy and ends up realizing she's very close to the person at the head of the conspiracy. As they sort through the puzzle, family ties come back to haunt each of them and the struggle to keep the balance of the war just slightly in their own favor pushes forward.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Strengths</u>
</b><br />1. Lisbeth and Blomkvist are as good as ever. They jump off the pages and yearn to be loved and hated at the same time. They annoy you, but you know they are good people. <br /><br />2. It's definitely a page-turner that captures your attention about 20% in when you realize how many different players are in the game to capture the technology and to double-cross one another. It stays strong and keeps you guessing throughout the whole story. And then the head of the conspiracy is revealed about 50% through, you have a whole new level of connections that keep your mind working over-time.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Suggestions</u>
</b><br />The summary of the story is strong, but the details get too technical and too convoluted. I work in technology, so it wasn't that I didn't understand what they were talking about... it was that so much of it was theory and advanced mathematical formulas, it got tedious to pay attention to that level of detail. There's only so much I can swallow when it comes to prime numbers and the Fibonacci sequence and how many multipliers are needed to deviate from the quantum... what??????? stick to the drama and leave the minutia out when you're trying to keep the sanctity of an author whose first successful novel was a genealogical mystery!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Final Thoughts</u>
</b><br />I enjoyed the book. I wanted to keep reading it. I'd like to see another one by this author. But... in order to move it up from a 3 to 4, it needs more substance. Hacking is a great topic. NSA double-crossing it a cool idea. The family ties (no spoilers here) was an amazing story line. But something felt like it was missing in how it truly all came together. I'm hoping it was left open so it can be explored in the next book -- not all to different from the original three in the series -- but it needs to be more tightly weaved. <br /><br />That said, kudos to Lagercrantz for successfully taking on the series and trying to continue the original creation. He's done well enough for me to continue reading but still to keep my critical eye.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17717263843317583025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Brenda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5240149-brenda"><img alt="Brenda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567952682p2/5240149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277645982?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda" href="/user/show/5240149-brenda">Brenda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277645982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11480464237598860237">I initially was going to give this 4 stars, but decided 3 more accurately represented my feelings. I found the first third of the book tedious and I almost gave up. Like all newspapers, Millenium is in trouble and purchased by a larger company. Mikael Blomkvist is unhappy and unmotivated. There were a lot of new characters introduced, and a refresher list of previous characters was provided in the beginning. The agencies and groups involved tended to get tangled, and it was difficult to remember</span>
  <span id="freeText11480464237598860237" style="display:none">I initially was going to give this 4 stars, but decided 3 more accurately represented my feelings. I found the first third of the book tedious and I almost gave up. Like all newspapers, Millenium is in trouble and purchased by a larger company. Mikael Blomkvist is unhappy and unmotivated. There were a lot of new characters introduced, and a refresher list of previous characters was provided in the beginning. The agencies and groups involved tended to get tangled, and it was difficult to remember who worked for who. Eventually, the story got interesting because Lisbeth Salander became more prominent. A weird web of intrigue involving police, the NSA, Swedish Intelligence, and assorted hackers was revealed along with the motivations of individuals involved. This was an acceptable effort by David Lagercrantz, but I would have liked more Salander right from the beginning.</span>

It was like a whole bunch of complicated cyber-hacking sounding plot lines were thrown in a blender and the mush that came out was put into print. The author tried too hard to carry on after Larsen.<br/><br/>I think the reason I still liked it a bit was that I know the characters from the previous books. If this was my first time with Blomkvist and Salander, I think I would have been very puzzled.</span>

<div id="review_1328915741" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1328915741" />
    <a title="Kristina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4272284-kristina"><img alt="Kristina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584248335p2/4272284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1328915741?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristina" href="/user/show/4272284-kristina">Kristina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=hated-em">hated-em</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=hyped">hyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=my-book">my-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=got-rid-of">got-rid-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=suck">suck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=omg-this-book-is-so-dumb">omg-this-book-is-so-dumb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1328915741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer300433402690959363">I’m not going to beat around the bush. This book is terrible. I suggest that if you really, really liked the first three, do not read this one. It’s poorly written. Nothing works. Not the plot, not the characters, not any of the words the author uses to describe what happens with the characters in the plot. I got to page 125 and decided I would just skim the rest because life is too short to read crappy books, but then I found myself reading more than skimming so I will count this book as “read.</span>
  <span id="freeText300433402690959363" style="display:none">I’m not going to beat around the bush. This book is terrible. I suggest that if you really, really liked the first three, do not read this one. It’s poorly written. Nothing works. Not the plot, not the characters, not any of the words the author uses to describe what happens with the characters in the plot. I got to page 125 and decided I would just skim the rest because life is too short to read crappy books, but then I found myself reading more than skimming so I will count this book as “read.” Stieg Larsson, the originator of these characters and author of the first three books, was no Shakespeare, but his writing was competent. His characters came to life on the page and his plots, although somewhat convoluted, were suspenseful and interesting and you cared about what happened. David Lagercrantz, the author of <i>The Girl in the Spider’s Web</i>, has no business continuing the story of Lisbeth Salander and Mikael Blomkvist and the other characters he carried over from the previous <i>Millennium</i> books. He’s not up to the challenge.<br /><br />Usually this is where I write a brief summary of the plot of the book. I’d love to do that, except I’m not quite sure what the hell the plot is. I think it’s actually a two plot book: there’s computer technology/corporate espionage and criminal internet gangs. There’s also Salander’s murky past coming back to bite her in the ass. The two plots are related. Also, side plots involving the financial downfall of <i>Millennium</i> (Blomkvist’s magazine) and an autistic boy whose artistic gifts really are the deus ex machina of the novel. Along with Salander’s superhero powers. Seriously. If Lagercrantz casually mentioned Salander leaping tall buildings in a single bound or flying around Sweden in a red cape, I would not have been surprised. As described in this novel, the woman is a superhero. And, yes, for anyone’s who already read the book, I know <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that I’m mixing up my superheroes. But I don’t know anything about Marvel Comics or their super people and I don’t give a rat’s ass. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I have many issues with this book and Salander the one-woman army is one of them. I’ll try to hide blatant spoilers, but if you really don’t want to know anything about this book, stop reading. <br /><br />My theory is that Lagercrantz was under so much pressure to stay true to the Lisbeth Salander character that he erred on the side of excessive character worship. This book presents Salander as a superhero who can do everything. I know in the past books she is a computer hacker genius and a badass, but it was believable. In this book, it’s ridiculous. I don’t even know why the other characters were in the book—Salander basically does everything. What’s so ironic is that even though this book is described as a “Lisbeth Salander” novel (as opposed to being a “Millennium” novel), she’s more talked <i>about</i> by other characters than she is actually present in the book. As a reader, I don’t see much of the story through her eyes, except perhaps tedious (for non-math lovers) lengthy discussions of prime numbers and other mathematical-related blah blah blah that I skipped because I just didn’t give a shit.<br /> <br />As I stated earlier, the plot is unclear. Hans Balder, some kind of computer internet genius, is introduced. He used to work in the US at some company called Solifon, but he left there to come home to Sweden and try to be a better father to his autistic son, August. When he moved to the US, he left his son with his ex-wife and her asshole boyfriend. She does care about August, but asshole boyfriend does not—he just wants the child support money. Asshole boyfriend, in keeping with past themes of “men acting badly towards women and children,” beats August and his mother. So Balder takes his child (even though legally he does not have custody) and stays in his nice house, trying to communicate with his silent child. He is nervous and worried because “someone” is out to get him. Meanwhile, people from the NSA and Säpo (Swedish top secret police) are discussing him and believe he is in danger. I had to read over one hundred pages just to get this information. Lagercrantz switches point of view between various characters, which would be fine if the story were more clear (and compelling). Eventually all the pieces fit together, but the payoff does not equal the effort of slogging through 400 pages. The only detail I gleaned from the novel that is important: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the ultimate villain is Camilla, Salander’s sister. Of course. It’s clear that there will be more “Lisbeth Salander” novels and that Camilla will be a recurring bad girl. Since I don’t plan on reading another of these books, I don’t care. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Lagercrantz should have done some basic police procedural research. His bad guys are boring and not very scary and rather incompetent. The police are also depicted as not being able to find their asses with both hands. It’s entirely unbelievable and I kept rolling my eyes and muttering curse words under my breath. That’s the whole novel—completely unbelievable. None of the characters have any complexity to them at all. None. The bad guys are <i>bad</i> and the good guys are <i>good</i>. There’s no muddying of the waters except perhaps with Lisbeth, but she’s depicted as such the righter of wrongs, a bad ass punk girl with the heart of gold who rescues women and boys from bullies who beat them, that even her grungy, hung-over, tattooed and pierced persona is a sugary frosting on her delectable self. It’s just so <i>gag</i>. I rarely enjoy novels of such simplistic morality. When I do (as I did the three earlier novels), the bad has to be <i>very</i> bad, so much so that I demand justice, even if the characters and their actions are so easily divided between black and white. In this novel, I’m underwhelmed by the bad guys. Sure, they’re jerks, but they’re bland jerks. So when Salander moves in to save the day (as she does many times), I’m lukewarm. Yah. She kicked ass…so what? <br /><br /><i>The Girl in the Spider’s Web</i> is not worthy of being connected with Stieg Larsson’s <i>Millennium</i> novels. It’s too bad that the publishers, lawyers, whomever, decided to make more money by carrying on the series. Lagercrantz is a mediocre writer with no gift for suspense or action sequences. While in theory he stays true to the characters, he portrays them with little imagination and no skill. This book does not carry on the legacy of Larsson’s earlier books. Not even close.<br /><br />While reading this book, I took almost ten pages of notes. Here are some highlights of my complaints:<br />1.	The whole Hans Balder is in danger nonsense. He knows he’s in danger and that “someone” is after him. But when Säpo calls and says they want to move him to a safe house, he refuses. When Säpo tries to get him special protection, no one’s available. But wait…I thought this guy was really really important? So instead Balder gets a police patrol, two incompetent jackasses who are more concerned with discussing a female colleague’s sweet, sweet ass instead of patrolling. When Balder’s alarm goes off and the security company calls him, they tell him to “go down to a special room in the cellar and lock the door” (101). Um, it’s called a panic room, Mr. Security Professional. Balder doesn’t do this. Then Mr. Security Professional tells Balder it’s all good because the guy wandering around his property is probably a junkie: “The man walks like a junkie—like a guy who’s just taken a load of speed. There’s something cocky and stilted about the way he moves, and that could be a sign that he’s just an ordinary druggie and petty thief” (101). Really? The intruder walks like a junkie so hey, no worries? What the fuck. So Balder, who is nervous, never goes to his “special room.” Even though he has received death threats. Even though his son is with him. Balder takes absolutely no sensible action to protect his life or the life of his son. Gee, guess what happens? This annoys the shit out of me because it’s obvious that the author has EVERYONE act like a flaming moron in order to make it easier for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the weirdo hitman to shoot Balder—but of course spare the kid. Why spare the kid? Oh, because Hitman knows that the kid is a “retard” and it’s a “breach of his professional ethics” to shoot retarded kids. He cares, even if he uses offensive language. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The police reaction is unbelievable. They don’t recognize the sound of gunfire? They have no emergency training? Of course not. That’s why they stand around like dumb fucks asking each other what to do. <br /><br />2.	August, the autistic boy wonder. I have no problem with the kid himself or his autism. What I have a problem with is how Lagercrantz turns the kid into the human equivalent of Lassie. What’s that girl? Who are the bad guys? Oh, you can draw pictures of amazing genius clarity that show the faces of the bad guys and the bad things they do? Oh, good girl, Lassie. I mean, August. How freaking convenient. And helpful since all the law enforcement officers in this novel have rocks for heads. <br /><br />3.	Lots of book-title-name dropping. Yes, we get it, Lagercrantz. You read books. You really like Elizabeth George. Goody for you.<br /><br />4.	Salander the Ultimate Bad Ass with the Heart of Gold. Jesus. What can’t she do? She’s hot (he is “one of the many in the gym who fancied Salander” 134) and has “nice tits” 188 (Really? Because in previous books she’s described as flat-chested and bony); she’s a chess wiz; she has hands so strong they crush drinking glasses (98 and “the uncanny strength of her hands” 191); she takes a bullet saving August and hijacks a moving car (“She was young with black hair and piercings, a punk according to one witness, also short, but fierce. The witnesses all agree that she was not some ordinary member of the public” 238); she’s a genius hacker with a style that has a “completely new threshold of originality” (272); she of course connects naturally with August and gets him to speak to her; she beats up and evicts the asshole boyfriend who beat August and August’s drug-addled and completely unsympathetic character of a mother; she saves August again from the hitman, notifies the police and neutralizes the threat all while protecting the kid AND standing on a crumbling rock ledge. It’s just too much. While all this is going on, Blomkvist is flirting with a woman whom he knows is bad news but she’s a puzzle he needs to figure out (eye roll—she’s the leader of the gang, moron) and the NSA and Säpo are standing around looking dazed. Well, no, the NSA is studying up on comics.<br /><br />5.	The <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Marvel Comics Connection. Are you fucking kidding me? Wasp, Salander’s hacker name, is a superhero in Marvel Comics. So, that’s why she acts like a superhero? Because she actually is one? And (I love this) the bad guys are part of a gang called the Spider Society—also in Marvel Comics. Guess who their enemies are? Guess. Guess. Okay. The “Sisterhood of the Wasp.” Wow. Could this be any stupider? It’s all about Marvel Comics. Wanna bet the author is a big ole comic book nerd? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />6.	The gross pseudo romance between Salander and Blomkvist (who I never liked. I didn’t like him in the previous books and he’s a dumb ass in this one). The author describes her as having a “flirty” tone or “flirting” with Blomkvist and what the fuck. Salander does not flirt. Gross.<br /><br />7.	The last sentence in the book: “A star fell outside in the night sky.” Please excuse me while I vomit on my keyboard. <br /><br />This book sucks. This book is awful. This book is flat out stupid. I don’t recommend it and I regret purchasing it. It will now go in my “get the fuck out of my house” pile of rejects. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="300433402690959363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
